  14. The Panasonic electric shaver is by far the most expensive shaver I, or my husband, have ever used!<br /><br />My husband has a Panasonic (similar to this model but with fewer blades) and a Norelco with the three, round, floating heads. After using this Panasonic, he says that he thinks the Norelco gives the closest dry shave, but this Panasonic gives the best wet shave he has ever had and that it is as smooth and close as a regular razor. I use it on my underarms, wet and dry, and it is definitely the best electric shaver I have ever used. CAUTION: The users manual says not to share this shaver with others for sanitary reasons and I would never share it with anyone but my husband of almost 40 years. Even then, I clean it carefully after each use.<br /><br />This is a foil-style electric shaver. There is a huge difference between rotary style shavers and foil style shavers and how you shave with them. The user manual says that it takes a month to get used to a new shaver and when I first read that, I thought it sounded crazy. It's not. Particularly if you are accustomed to using a regular razor or a rotary style shaver. My husband felt this shaver didn't give as close a shave initially compared to his old shaver, but now after two weeks, he feels he gets an exceptional shave with it. I would caution anyone considering this shaver to understand that you may not be happy with your shave at first and to realize that any new shaver requires a commitment of daily use for at least a couple of weeks before deciding if you are pleased with it.<br /><br />The shaving head is quite large and pivots in two directions, however you can lock the head so that it is stationary. My husband has found that locking the head is very helpful for shaving under the chin and neck. It is fairly loud, but not unpleasantly so. The handle is extremely comfortable. There is a pop-up trimmer that works fine - nothing special but does the job. There is a digital read-out on the handle which tells you how long each shave takes and how much battery life is left. (I thought the timer for how long your shave lasted was silly, but my husband and sons think it's cool.)<br /><br />The recharging/cleaning dock is one of the features that make this an exceptional shaving system. It will take up some real estate on your counter. It measures 3 3/4\\"W x 5 1/4\\"D x 7 3/4\\"T with the shaver in the charging position. But it will charge, clean and dry your shaver for you with just the touch of a button. The shaver is held head down in the charging/cleaning/drying position via magnetic contacts. It takes about an hour to fully charge this shaver. Note: you can also plug the power cord directly into the bottom of the shaver, which is good for traveling because the cleaning station would be bulky and messy to transport.<br /><br />The head sits in a well that fills with cleaning solution when you initiate the cleaning process. The cleaning process automatically sets the shaver to sonic cleaning mode several times while it is cleaning. When cleaning is complete, a fan dries your shaver with heated air. Drying is important in my experience with foil shavers because it extends the life of the foils. The solid cleaning solution is in a small cartridge that you slide into the bottom of the cleaning station. It should last about 6 months. The back of the cleaning station has a slide out reservoir that you fill with water used to dissolve the cleaning solution.<br /><br />You can also clean this shaver by applying liquid soap to the foils and then setting your shaver to sonic cleaning mode. It produces a lot of foam and then you can remove the foil head and rinse the shaver clean. The emphasis on cleaning is important because regular cleaning keeps the blades sharp longer, prolongs the life of the foils, provides a closer and more comfortable shave, and is more sanitary to avoid minor skin infections. Cleanliness really IS next to godliness when it comes to shaving.<br /><br />Also included is a custom fitted, zippered travel pouch and a snap-on plastic foil head protector.<br /><br />Clearly this razor is a premium product at a premium price. Is it worth it? I would say that it depends upon whether or not it is comfortably within your budget. You will get a fine shave and the cleaning/charging station makes the whole process completely effortless, but the price seems a little high to me based upon other shavers with similar features.uded is a custom fitted, zippered travel pouch and a snap-on plastic foil head protector.<br /><br />Clearly this razor is a premium product at a premium price.   15. Right when you think you've got the best razor out there, somebody has to go and come out with something 3x as expensive. The question then, is it 3x better? Let's find out.<br /><br />So I've been using the Braun 790cc razor for over about 19 months. I know this because I just replaced my blade at the 18 month mark about two months ago. This ensures it had a fair comparison with the Panasonic, as it was obviously brand new. This is also my first Panasonic. I've been using various high-end Braun razors for many years. Once they were worn out, I replaced them with whatever was the latest and greatest. I like my high-end razors. But when I saw this razor was retailing for $600, I was naturally skeptical that it was worth the price. Fortunately, this was a review unit, as you can see.<br /><br />First, out of the box you have all of the usual expected items. Razor, blade, cleaning system, refill cartridge, etc. This is all basic, so I won't go into too much detail. You just plug it in, charge, shave, clean. Repeat. I've been doing this for about a month to give it a fair comparison. They also suggest using a new razor for a month to allow your face to get used to it. However, compared to the Braun 790cc, which also had a fresh blade, there was really no adjustment.<br /><br />That's mostly because they use a similar cutting system. Except the Braun has a single larger cutter and the Panasonic uses 5 smaller ones. But not small enough. The head on the Panasonic is nearly twice as large as the Braun. Which is great for saving time on shaving most of your face, but it does make it more difficult to get into the tighter areas such as between the eye brows or under the nose. The head pivots in any direction that you'd like. Personally I've never found that to be as useful as it sounds. For everything else, the Panasonic wins, albeit by a slight margin. We're talking about a few seconds less shave time in favor of the 5-blade cutting system of the Panasonic.<br /><br />How about noise and comfort? First thing you'll notice when you turn it on is that the Panasonic is much, much quieter than the 790cc. It also vibrates much less. Braun uses this \\"feature\\" as a selling point claiming it's supposed to help shaving. I always found it slightly annoying, but it is something I've gotten used to over the years. The Panasonic is quiet enough that you can really hear it cutting each hair (and letting you know you missed some spots). It's also slightly smoother and just a little nicer to use on a regular basis. Another win for the Panasonic.<br /><br />Ergonomics. Braun wins. Between the unusual large head, slim body, and lack of a place to grasp it, the Panasonic is a little awkward to hold and switch positions. Sure, you do get used to it. But the Braun is much easier to hold in various position. I also keep finding that I'm pushing on the trimmer because it's right behind the head, where you hold it. Win for the Braun.<br /><br />Miscellaneous features? The trimmer works comparably well. Although the Panasonic's trimmer only likes going in one direction, otherwise it'll try to close. Neither are the easiest to maneuver around your face, but they get the job done. How about the cleaning system? Well, that's easy. The Panasonic wins here. It's quieter (thanks to a quieter razor) and it's nice enough to dry your razor after cleaning it. You also don't have that alcohol smell that you're left with the Braun. Both Razors also have LCD's with interesting information that's nice to have. But certainly something you could live without. Especially with the Panasonic as it has no memory and only displays battery/shaving time for a few seconds. The Panasonics display looks nicer.<br /><br />Let's wrap this up with some Pro's and Con's for the Panasonic.<br /><br />Pros:<br /><br />* Quiet and Smooth<br />* 5-blade cutting system works<br />* Cool looking blue LCD display<br />* Every feature you could want in a razor<br />* Fast and effective cutting<br/>* Improved cleaning & drying system<br /><br />Cons:<br /><br />* Crazy expensive<br />* Awkward ergonomics<br />* LCD display could be more useful<br />* Trimmer tends to close when moving \\"upward\\"<br /><br />So here's the tricky part. Who wins? Based on the features and performance listed in the review, The Panasonic easily wins. But price versus performance, the Braun wins. While the Panasonic does have the clear edge in features and performance, it's not enough to justify a $600 price tag when you can have an excellent Braun 7-series for around $200. I could easily go back to the Braun and not lose any sleep over it.<br /><br />However, if you are in fact looking for the best razor money can buy, the Panasonic is the way to go. Not to mention I can only assume the price will go down on this one fairly soon. In either case, I know I'll certainly continue using the Panasonic over the Braun.<br /><br />*** UPDATE 5/16 ***<br /><br />I just wanted to provide a quick update after some more time with the shaver. First, the shaver has been working great. I've just been servicing the cleaning system and replacing the filter as needed and it still works good as the day I got it. I have found that it works best if I start with a quick dry shave and complete a \\"final pass\\" with a wet shave.<br /><br />That seems to help reduce the number of \\"passes\\" along the skin and reduce irritation. Something you obviously can't do with dry-only shavers. The only negative, which was mentioned in the first review, is that darn trimmer. If you move upward, it keeps closing, unless you make sure to keep your finger on it. Which isn't super convenient given it's ergonomics.<br /><br />Otherwise, still a minor issue, but I just like to follow up with these type of reviews. Enjoy!
  16. Its been 30 days since I received and began using my Panasonic shaver. I thought I owned a very good Braun Series 7, and seriously doubted that anything could be much better, even at three times the price. I've owned my current Braun for at least 5 years, and have always been a foil shaver user, although I've tested (and quickly given up on) a decent rotary shaver by Norelco, foil works best for me.<br /><br />The first time I turned on the Panasonic, it sounded like a turbocharged version of my old razor - the Panasonic's F-18 whine made the poor old Braun sound like some poorly tuned Briggs and Stratton weedeater.<br /><br />As expected, the first shave was a bit awkward. Since my Braun has a skinnier head, and the Panasonic is much wider, the actual movement required is different and takes some getting used to. Also the Panasonic tilts on two axis - allowing virtually any rotation, where the Braun only tilts front/back. Each day I became more accustomed with to how to hold it and my shave time became more effective.<br /><br />The Panasonic got down to work right away with such speed and power that there was no tugging or pulling of my whiskers. After each shave, the razor tells you how long you've been using it and how much charge is left by percentage (by 10% increments). It will flash at ten percent for a about a day, and because it's digital, will go from full power to nothing instantly - as opposed to the Braun which will wind down slowly on the final day of shaving. Both last exactly 7 days between charges for me.<br /><br />After about 3 weeks of Panasonic use, I decided to take my Braun with us on a short vacation, allowing me to have a great chance to really compare the two shavers. Another reason to take the Braun is that the Panasonic only comes with a soft case, where the Braun's case is hard, which I feel is better protection. Sorrowfully, my old Braun made me feel like I'd gone back in time, driving a Model T instead of a 2012 Mercedes. It really was that different. Just like a faithful trooper, the Braun worked, but didn't give me as close or quick a shave as the Panasonic. I'd say the Panasonic takes me about 20% less time to shave and gives me about 25% better results.<br /><br />The wet or dry option with the Panasonic is definitely useful, and something I've never had the pleasure of experiencing before. I admit, it felt very strange taking an electric razor into the shower with me, and it's not something I'd do every day, but definitely gives a closer and more comfortable shave.<br /><br />Although it's nice to have an automatic cleaning and charging system (housed a strangely ugly and cheap-looking unit), it is also exceptional to have a razor that doesn't require expensive fluids to keep it clean. With a squirt of liquid soap, a special power setting, and a splash of water, the razor is clean and ready for another week of shaving duties. Not only does this save money, it's especially helpful for travelers who don't really feel like lugging the cleaning unit around (a messy proposition, even if you had space in the suitcase).<br /><br />The Panasonic did not disappoint me, and I feel it lived up to everything I believed a very expensive shaver should be. With a beautiful blue digital readout, nicely ergonomic handle, and great results, I really hope this shaver lasts the rest of my life, since I would truly be hard pressed to pay this much for a replacement!ul trooper, the Braun worked, but didn't give me as close or quick a shave as the Panasonic. With a squirt of liquid soap, a special power setting, and a splash of water, the razor is clean and ready for another week of shaving duties. Not only does this save money, it's especially helpful for travelers who don't really feel like lugging the cleaning unit around (a messy proposition, even if you had space in the suitcase). The Panasonic did not disappoint me, and I feel it lived up to everything I believed a very expensive shaver should be. With a beautiful blue digital readout, nicely ergonomic handle, and great results, I really hope this shaver lasts the rest of my life, since I would truly be hard pressed to pay this much for a replacement!

  34. I've have been a big fan of \\"linear\\" shavers since I purchased my first Panasonic Linear shaver about 15 years ago. Panasonic seemed to dominate the market for many years, but then Braun came out with a very nice version a few years ago (Braun calls them \\"Pulsonic\\" shavers), and suddenly the Braun Pulsonic shavers were the top selling models. I also currently have the Braun 790cc, their top of the line model, so comparing it against this top of the line Panasonic was an interesting showdown. Base station: Both units have a nice base station used for cleaning and recharging the unit. Both do a fine job. I was a little skeptical at first about the utility of a base station, but now I'm sold. Dealing with cords and plugs is annoying. I really appreciate the convenience of dropping the shaver in and having it automatically cleaned and recharged. Articulation: Both units have an articulating head which maintain an optimal angle of attack against your skin. The Braun only pivots forward and backward, however, while the Panasonic also moves side to side. Both do a fine job of maintaining good blade contact, and the additional benefit from Panasonic's side to side movement is minor. Closeness of shave: First of all, both models provide a very close shave. That's why so many people love these shavers. Just as close as shaving with a blade, and much more convenient. I often shave while surfing the web (in fact, I was shaving while writing this review). It's recommended to shave before taking a shower so that you take advantage of the natural lubricants your skin produces on your face, so shaving while reading the morning news online is my typical routine. After using both shavers for at least a month, I find that the Panasonic will shave slightly closer. Not sure if that is due to the additional blades the Panasonic has, or the faster drive system (the Panasonic vibrates at 14,000 per second while the Braun is 10,000). However, the Braun is still very close. Skin burn: Zero. Both of these shavers produce no irritation for me. Even after I've basically finished shaving, I can do additional passes with the shaver, over and over the smooth skin searching for that last bit of hair to remove, and my skin doesn't get irritated. Vibration: Here is finally a category where there is a substantial difference. The Braun vibrates quite a bit. It's not annoying at all, in fact I find it relaxing, but your milage may vary. The vibration produces more sound (more on that below), but some people suggest that it is beneficial. For example, my girlfriend uses one of these: [[ASIN:B0009F402K Clarisonic Classic Skincare Brush - White]] which is specifically designed to vibrate your facial skin to exfoliate dead cells and promote circulation. So, the Braun's vibrations may actually help your skin stay more youthful. Noise: The Panasonic is definitely more smooth and sounds more refined than the Braun. I got out my Radio Shack sound level meter to measure the difference in volume. At 4\\" (roughly the average distance the shaver will be from your ears during operation) the Panasonic is 73 dB while the Braun is 78 dB. Thus, the Braun is 10^((78-73)/10) = 3.16 times louder than the Panasonic. The Braun isn't deafening by any means, but I appreciate the more quite and refined sound of the Panasonic. Price: Currently, the Panasonic is about 2x the Braun. That's not a small difference. In summary, the Panasonic delivers the smoothest shave with a more refined experience. The Braun also delivers a smooth shave, along with some vibration that some people may want, but also with some noise.

  36. I'm one of the minority of reviewer's who actually purchased this product (*definitely increasing since I wrote this though!); I didn't pay full retail (still listed some places as just south of $600), so let's say a little over half that. And the replacement head/foil is 80 bucks. So my comments straight up relate to whether I think I got my money's worth, not just the technical aspects of the shaver. The short version if you don't want to read the list is, yes, I think I did, with a footnote.<br /><br />I've used just about every new model electric shaver out there in the quest for the perfect shaver, and reviewed several of them here: [[ASIN:B003YJAZZ4 Braun Series 7- 790cc Pulsonic Shaver System, Silver]], [[ASIN:B003V32UDI Philips Norelco 1290x/40 SensoTouch 3d Electric Shaver, Black]], [[ASIN:B002N5MHLK Panasonic ES-LA93-K Men's 4-Blade (Arc 4) Multi-Flex Dual-Motor Wet/Dry Nanotech Rechargeable Electric Shaver with Vortex Cleaning System, Black]]. To cut to the chase, there isn't a perfect shaver, at least one that fits everyone's shaving style. This one comes pretty darn close.<br /><br />First the obvious: this is a foil shaver. If you use a rotary shaver and are happy with the results, stop reading and/or get the Norelco; it's the best one out there. A rotary shave is completely and totally different than a foil experience. If you think there might be something better, read on.<br /><br />Second, among foils there are dry shavers only, and those that are both wet and dry. The LV81 is both. The Braun above is dry only. If you like to shave dry only, the Braun will serve you as well as any in my opinion, and has a superior cleaning system to the Panny, as well as costing a lot less. If you like a dry electric shave and don't care to change, get the Braun. If you think there might be something better, read on.<br /><br />The ES-LV81 is the successor to the ES-LA93 (which I was using immediately prior and it was pretty good) and a worthy successor it is. It's the best wet electric shaver I have ever used. Ever. Things Panasonic has improved over the LA93:<br /><br />- The constantly flashing blue police-cruiser charging light is gone; when the cleaning/charging cycle is complete, the unit goes off (cleaner and shaver). Some might miss it; me - not.<br /><br />- The shaver is quieter than the LA93, both in use and during the cleaning cycle. Significantly less to my ear, but the previous model Panasonic shaver itself was already quieter than the Braun, although none of them are anywhere near as quiet as a rotary.<br /><br />- A faster shave. The larger head really is functional, and if you already use the LA93 the transition will be seamless. It's more like gently scrubbing your face with a pad rather than shaving, and less irritating since you don't need to move the head as much over the same area. The larger head covers a lot of ground quickly, and I've reduced my shaving time by 30-40%. There is a shaving timer in the display, which I actually like - I've had one on other shavers; it helps me improve my shaving technique and speed up to a point of diminishing returns. The popup trimmer is functionally the same as the LA93.<br /><br />- The cleaning station looks almost identical to the one for the LA93 externally (other than the silver front); in fact, the LV81 actually fits in the old one (sort of), but it's apparently a completely different unit. The interior well seems to be deeper; the back is contoured differently to fit the LV81, the cleaning cartridge fits flush rather than inset, and it does seem to be quieter. It also seems like the cleaning cycle is shorter, but I haven't timed it. When the cleaning cycle is complete, the lights go out, unlike the LA93 unit where the green LEDs for Clean/Dry flash continuously. It does use the same cartridges, and the water reservoirs appear to be the same. Noisier than the Braun or Norelco cleaners - and it runs longer - it does what it's supposedto do, and very economically as well.<br /><br />So is it worth three hundred and a half bills to upgrade from the earlier Panasonic? To me, yes - I knew what I was getting, and it's really a significant improvement over any other Panasonic. Is it worth it to switch from another system or manufacturer? That depends.... If you THINK you might want to switch from a blade or a rotary experience, or switch to a wet shave from a dry with a different foil, I think a good price point would be in the $200+ range, which this shaver will eventually hit within a few months I would guess, and you might not feel too bad about switching back if it didn't work out. At today's price point, if you have the bucks and want to experiment, I think you'll be pleasantly surprised.<br /><br />If you haven't tried it, a wet electric shave with a foil shaver is (to me) the closest, most comfortable electric shave you can get - and with this shaver, as close as you're going to get to a blade with an electric in my opinion. If you've been searching for the perfect electric, this just might be it.to do, and very economically as well.<br /><br />So is it worth three hundred and a half bills to upgrade from the earlier Panasonic? If you've been searching for the perfect electric, this just might be it.

A couple benefits I didn't mention before: No nicks! And no smell of shaving cream if you shave dry. So I still stand by my originalconclusion, a razor works better and is cheaper. But there are applications for an electric, and this is a great electric.or an electric, and this is a great electric.

You're supposed to replace the water and the cartridge at the same time and the cartridge can last up to two months. The thought of two month old water and beard shavings \\"cleaning\\" my shaver doesn't make sense. Instead, I clean the razor out in the shower with a quick rinse after each shave and then use the \\"dry\\" cycle on the dock to make the sure the razor doesn't rust or get funky. A quick warning: The dry cycle on the unit takes some THREE HOURS for some reason. That's gotta put a dent in your electricity bill at some point. In any case, the performance of the shaver is great. the blades whip a bit of shave gel into a nice soft lather and it glides across your face. The side burn trimmer could be better but I don't use it too often. It's a great shaver but is it worth the price? $600 (MSRP) is a little ridiculous for any shaver and I'd try some lower level wet electric shavers before making the investment.

Buy the Panasonic ES-LA63 instead of the LV81K and get as good a shave...and pocket the $450 difference (that'll pay for most of the price of an IPAD).

After using the 8000 series for 5 years, it stopped holding the blade in place properly, lost its ability to shave close. I figured I would stay with Braun since I liked the 8000 series so much, so I bought their current generation 5-series, the middle line of their 3, 5, and 7-series. While the Braun 5 was quieter than the prior gen, it also felt slower, and it definitely did not shave as well. I had trouble with the fleshier parts of my neck, even when stretching skin. Enter the Panasonic ES-LV81-K, provided by Amazon. The shaver has an led display that will show you the run-time while you're shaving...interesting information, but not essential. I typically finish shaving face, neck, back of neck within 3 minutes with this shaver, if that's important to anyone. To get this kind of shave with the Braun 5-series would take probably at least a minute longer. The display also shows the battery level, definitely useful information. The Panasonic shaver is a bit noisy, but no more than I would have expected from an electric. If their option to make it quieter was to slow down the oscillations, then I would eagerly choose the noise. A feature in the Braun that I liked, their cleaning solution was alcohol-based, and I would run it after each shave, to keep bacteria from forming. I do similarly with the Panasonic, run the cleaning cycle after each shave. You fill a reservoir with probably around 4 ounces of tap water, or distilled water if you like, plug in the small Panasonic cleaning cartridge, and it's ready to go for a month or two of cleaning cycles.A feature I like in the Panasonic, they follow the Clean cycle with a Dry cycle, so the shaver is dry the next time you go to use it. The Braun passively air-dried, and there were times that it still had the cleaning solution dripping from it when I went to use it. Not an issue with the Panasonic, it ends up bone dry. The cleaning cycle takes around 5 minutes to complete, and the razor runs intermittently during that time, followed by a few minutes of a fan blowing air during the Dry cycle. That's a lot of detail, maybe a waste of time to some readers of this review, but let me cut to the chase. If I accidentally dropped this razor in the toilet, or on a concrete floor, to where I had to replace it, I would DEFINITELY seek out another Panasonic just like this one. I had my latest Braun for around 3 months, and I was not happy with it all, was wanting to try some other brand. The timing of arrival for this Panasonic was perfect. After using the Panasonic now for around 3 weeks, I am thoroughly satisfied. I wanted to live with it for some time before posting my review, and I honestly could not imagine another electric giving me a closer shave than this Panasonic ES-LV81-K. I realize it's a bit pricey, which may put off some buyers, but if your budget will allow, or can be stretched a bit, I can not recommend this Panasonic any more highly. It's an outstanding shaver. PRO: - Comfortable shave - Very close shave - Wide cutting path - Fast blade frequency - Powerful - Articulating head - Cleaning station - Clean and Dry cycles - Water-washable - Travel pouch included CON: - Wouldn't mind if the housing was thicker, not as slender. I have large hands, and the slender shape of the housing takes some getting used to. - A tad pricey

I thought the Braun was great and I'd never used an electric shaver like the Braun before but it wasn't quite perfect. I tend not to write my reviews for products right after I start using them. I find that given time a product's true faults and benefits really become obvious. Sometimes they're things that are easy to miss while in the honeymoon phase. So here we go... the Panasonic ES-LV81-K is the best electric shaver I have ever used. It's also the most expensive so it comes down to a cost vs. benefit decision. Given that I tend to keep my shavers for 3-4 years it's an easy decision for me because this is a tool that I use almost every day. Here are some pros and cons to make things simple: Good stuff * Fast. The 5 blades cover a lot of surface area at once * Wet/Dry system. Usable in the shower * Self-cleaning system that requires soap and water and nothing else. So you're not stuck using the Vortex Cleaning System and Cartridges * Minimal irritation. Not sure what it is but it doesn't chew up my skin * Cleaning cartridges don't contain alcohol and that means less irritation. They're also cheaper than the Braun's and ship by air Bad Stuff * Expensive. Did I say that before? $450+ for a shaving system? * Very large shaving head so it's not that maneuverable. I have a tough time shaving the area under my nose and getting my sideburns quite right * Single option for cleaning. I got used to the Braun's which had light and deep cleanings. That's about it. When it comes to products that I receive from Amazon Vine it's quite simple... if I'm using it after 2 months then I love it. If I'm not and it's been relegated to the garage then... Even at $450+ I think this is a great shaver and I've never used anything quite like it. When that price (don't forget to add the cleaning cartridges if you use them and the replacement blade) is amortized over a few years and the fact that most of us guys will use a shaver almost every day it's expensive but not that crazy if you're getting something that you can't get elsewhere. I'd give it 5 stars but at this price the lack of maneuverability is something that you shouldn't have to deal with.

  65. Hitherto trying the Panasonic ES-LV81K, I didn't even know manufacturers made $600 electric shavers. $600 you say, that's crazy! Yes, I thought so too until I used the Panasonic. I've primarily been a manual shaver man most of my life, bouncing from the early Mach 3s, to Remingtons, and then my trusty Fusion. My last electric shaver was a $90 Norelco 1150X, which I thought was pricey for a shaver. I had a bad experience with the Norelco, despite being advertised as being able to dry shave, was never able to do so without irritating my sensitive skin. Moreover, I found the Norelco had a tendency to shave off large patches of hair, in a particularly uneven manner. So my faith in electric shavers was shaken until the Panasonic... EXTERIOR DESIGN: The first feature you'll notice about the Panasonic is the particularly strikingly large head, comprising 5-blades. It reminds me of the Mach-3/Quattro/Fusion manual razor wars, where each manufacturer would try to up the other in terms of the number of blades. However on the Panasonic, the 5 blades aren't a gimmick, they do wonders. The blades are encased in a head, which has an easily removable outer casing, which exposes the inner blades for cleaning. Depress two buttons on each side of the head, and the outer casing pops right off. The head freely rotates, though somewhat limited in its side-to-side and back and forth motion. The rotation was more than suitable for my shaving needs. The head also mounts an integrated trimmer which is easily locked into place by a selector mounted below. The shaver is a sleek black (not as nice looking as the gun-metal dark blue on its cheaper ES-LV61 brother in my opinion), and is not a bright tacky light blue like on the Norelco. The body is finished in a 3/4 slip-resistant & fingerprint resistant material, which is comfortable to hold. The body is also contoured for a comfortable grip. There is a chrome circular selector switch that toggles between operating mode andtravel lock mode. Lastly, a display screen with bright blue LED digits shows battery life, minutes/seconds the shaver was in use (a helpful feature), charge status, etc.. The LED display is very bright, and easy to read, even in a pitch black room. The razor recharges with an AC adapter connected to its base; alternatively, the ES-LV81K can be recharged when plugged into the provided cleaning station. The biggest downside of the Panasonic is that it requires replacement of the blades every 1-2 years, though I expect those who are less hirsute can observe a more lax replacement program. These replacement blades don't come cheap either, at least $50-70 (which is about standard for electric shavers; IIRC, replacement Norelco blades were about that much too). If you want a cost-effective system, stick with manual razors. If you're putting down five benjamins for this system, then replacement blade costs probably aren't going to deter you from making the purchase. It's a solid, good looking razor (more on the cleaning station later). OPERATION: The Panasonic only needs 1 hour charging time, before full operation. A quick 5-10 minute charge will get you maybe 1-2 shaves. The ES-LV81K emits a solid, high pitched whine when in use. The 14,000 cpm and 5 blades is no joke here. I was able to dry shave WITHOUT SKIN IRRITATION. That's a first for me, as I have sensitive skin which I usually have to slap with copious amounts of aftershave following each session. My post dry-shave session was incredible, didn't even feel like I had just shaved. I also tried the Panasonic with a wet-shave, and was able to achieve an amazingly close shave. Remember the old adage that an electric shaver will never be able to replicate the results of a manual blade or razor? The Panasonic completely destroys that adage. I feel as smooth as the proverbial baby's posterior. The Panasonic also allows shaving in the shower. The trimmer works no differently, and I was able to get a smooth trim on my sideburns. The LV81 is also very easy to clean. Add a little dishwashing liquid or liquid soap to the outer blades, hold down the power button to activate the \\"sonic vibration mode\\", at which point the razor self-cleans. I also used a toothbrush to remove some small hairs that had deposited on the base of the inner blades. SELF-CLEANING RECHARGER STATION: The primary difference between the ES-LV81K and the $100 cheaper ES-LV61 is the addition of a self-cleaning recharger station. The station is a cradle for both recharging the LV81K, and for holding the LV81K during cleaning. A detergent pack is provided, and one just has to fill up a mini-water tank before selecting a cleaning option. The cleaning process takes 10 minutes, at which point it engages in an 80 minute drying process, then a post-recharge. The cleaning station has a little too much tacky plastic for my tastes considering the price of the system, but at least it seems solidly built and fingerprint proof. During cleaning, the station emits several loud beeps every 30 seconds, which can be annoying. The station is the answer to every lazy man's question. If you can't be bothered to self-clean the razor with its built-in sonic mode vibration system and are also OCD about having the razor dried at 170 degrees C, then buy the system. Otherwise, save yourself $100 and get the cheaper and nearly identical LV61. Minus one star because the LV81K is a poorer value than the LV61, and Panasonic's MSRP is a bit outrageous. OVERALL THOUGHTS: Is the Panasonic expensive? Yes, but it certainly lives up to its claims and provides an amazing shave. Cue heavenly music playing from above. There is one caveat, this LV61 shaver is not interchangeable with the shaver on the LV81 cleaning/docking system; the LV61 is missing three electrodes on the rear of the body which allow charging with the cleaning/docking system.

I have used both rotary and vibrating type razors of the years with about the same level of success with each. The Panasonic ES-LV81 is a \\"shaving system\\" on an entirely different level than I am used to, but it was worth the trip.<br /><br />The shaver itself is very comfortable to hold and has a lock on the power switch - as someone who has had electric razors start up in his luggage while traveling, I appreciate this a lot. The business end of the shaver has five blades, but if you pull off the head you see only two. Three more are hidden inside the head. This model is said to have an improved foil design that lifts hairs better than the previous generation. The head normally swivels in two directions, but you can lock it in place if you want. The third position on the swivel lock switch pops up a small trimmer for mustaches, etc. I liked that in use I could actually see the trimmer blade in the mirror, unlike on most shavers.<br /><br />The actual shaving bit was wonderful - it sounds like an angry hornet but it does an excellent job of shaving. I was especially interested in trying it in the shower, something I had never done before. This model is waterproof and I was impressed with how well it performed in the shower.<br /><br />You can charge the shaver two ways - by connecting the power cord directly to the shaver, or by connecting the cord to the cleaning dock and inserting the shaver, blades down, into the dock. The dock can dry the shaver (which you'd want to do after using it in the shower) - this runs a fan for three hours.<br /><br />The dock can also clean the shaver. This uses a water tank you clip on the back and a detergent cartridge that slips in underneath. When you activate the cleaning cycle, water cycles through the detergent sponge and enters a reservoir in which the blades are sitting. The dock causes the shaver to oscillate the blades at low speed and then at \\"sonic\\" speed, at intervals. At the end of the wash, it enters the dry cycle. After either a clean/dry or dry cycle, it charges. You can select clean/dry/charge, dry/charge or just charge. The detergent cartridge is said to last for about six months - at that time you dump the water, rinse the tank and then refill, along with replacing the cartridge. I tested the cleaning and it worked well.<br /><br />You can also clean the shaver by pulling off the head and rinsing the blades under running water, pressing and holding the power switch to enable the \\"sonic\\" cleaning mode. The head just rinses off normally, then dry the shaver. Now that I've had the shaver a few months, this is the cleaning method I tend to use most. It certainly takes less time than using the automatic cleaner, and works just as well.<br /><br />The dock is quite large and you will need to make room for it on a table or shelf. I was amused to note that the manual warned against using the dock or plugging in the razor in a bathroom. I am not sure why this is - the power cord has a small switching wall-wart on the plug end, and it is universal voltage. Maybe it's the lack of a ground-fault interrupter that makes it unsuitable for bathroom use? I expect most users to ignore this.<br /><br />I really liked the Panasonic ES-LV81 and it gave me the best shave I have ever experienced. If you're willing to pay the price, you'll get a superb product. (A note on the price - I have observed that when Amazon doesn't have the product in stock, it shows the list price, but when it is in stock, the price is significantly lower. Even at the lower price I have seen, that's a lot of money for a shaver in my opinion.)speed and then at \\"sonic\\" speed, at intervals. At the end of the wash, it enters the dry cycle.   113. I've been shaving since the 1960's. I've used blades with shaving cream and electrics. Virtually all of my electrics have been made by Braun or Norelco. The Panasonic ES-LV81 is the best electric shaver I've ever used. I've been using the ES-LV81 for just over a month and have a few observations based on that experience. - As good as it is, I'd have trouble justifying the purchase for myself. When I mentioned it to my dermatologist, he compared it to cosmetic surgery: you have to decide for yourself if it's worth the cost for the benefits you expect to receive. On the other hand, I think almost anyone who shaves on a regular basis would welcome this as a gift. - The ES-LV81 is both larger and heavier than I expected. This is not to say that it's ungainly or hard to handle, just different from the Norelcos and Brauns I've used in the past. It feels solid and well-made (the razor is made in Japan, the cleaning base is made in China). - The thing that most surprised me: I experienced no discomfort or irritation from the first use several weeks ago on through this morning. There was no break-in period for me. The last time I moved from one Norelco to a newer (3-4 years) version of the same model, I suffered irritation on my neck for about ten days. There is a 30-Day satisfaction guarantee and an entreaty to please stick with it for 30 days. - The reason I chose the ES-LV81 over the ES-LV61 was that I was curious about the cleaning system. The self-cleaning recharger does exactly what it is intended to do: it throughly cleans the razor and then charges it. It tried using it once a day and then every four or five days; the cleaning performance was the same in either case. I do think the self-cleaning recharger would make a good project for a talented industrial designer; to my eye it's bulky, unattractive, and retro (and not cool retro, just out of date). The self-cleaning recharger uses a proprietary detergent cartridge which is good for about 30 cleanings. Three-packs are currently available from Amazon for about ten dollars and are available under the Subscribe & Save program, which takes 15% off the price at the time of shipping. - The self-cleaning recharger is kind of noisy. You definitely would want to start it in the morning before you leave the house and not at bedtime. - One thing I like about the ES-LV81 is that, while it may be a little louder than some other electrics, I can clearly hear the sound of individual whiskers being chopped off. This is great for places like my neck and below my jawline; I just keep going until I don't hear any more cutting instead of relying on a mirror and my middle-aged eyes. My experience is that whiskers on my neck are less likely to be cut with an electric if they are missed and grow out even a little. I've always had to touch up my neck every few days with a conventional razor. I have not had to do this since using the ES-LV81. I did try it a blade touch-up a couple of times in the shower, but found none of the 1/8\\" or longer whiskers that usually turned up in my Gillette Fusion in the past. - Panasonic specifies liquid hand soap to clean the shaver if you choose not the use or cannot use the self-cleaning recharger (a travel case for the shaver is included). Instructions are both in the manual and on a separate insert. - Panasonic recommends changing the outer foil once a year and replacing the inner blades every other year. These parts are not yet widely available in the US. The foil can be found for about sixty dollars and the blades for about thirty-five dollars. A combo pack is about eighty dollars. I would expect to see lower prices as they become available from more retail outlets, including Amazon. It would be foolish to buy such a high quality device and not maintain it. It's also true that you could buy a new lower-end Norelco or Braun every other year for about the cost of foils and blades for the ES-LV81. This is not a casual purchase, but it seems to be a quality product that should have a long useful life if properly maintained.

  120. In the world of electric razors there are two basic types: The foil type (like those made by Braun and Panasonic). And the rotary type (like those made by Norelco). I've used Norelco razors for many years. They shave well and they're easy to clean. My old Norelco burned up (literally), and I thought I'd try a foil-type razor again just to see if there was anything I was missing.<br /><br />Noise: The first thing I noticed is that this razor is a lot louder than a Norelco. This isn't a deal breaker for me, but it's worth mentioning if noise is an issue.<br /><br />Ease of shaving: For the neck and cheek area it's great. But the Panasonic is not as easy to use around the chin when compared to a Norelco. Specifically, I think Norelco razors follow contoured areas of the face with less effort.<br /><br />Ergonomics: This razor isn't as easy to hold and maneuver as a traditional type Norelco razor. When I say a &#34;traditional&#34; type, I mean the older style Norelco razors they've been making for decades, and not the newer Norelco SensoTouch series. In my opinion, the Norelco SensoTouch razors are a far cry ergonomically from the easy-to-hold shape of the traditional Norelco razor.<br /><br />Closeness: This razor shaves very smooth and close. But then again, I don't think it shaves any more smoothly or any closer than Norelco razors costing a fourth as much.<br /><br />Ease of cleaning: I have no interest in using cleaning systems. They may be convenient in some ways, but I'd rather not have to periodically clean the cleaning system or replenish it with special cleaning fluids. I prefer to clean electric razors myself using hot running water, soap, and/or isopropyl alcohol. Overall, I think the traditional Norelco razor is a little easier to clean.<br /><br />Other thoughts: The workmanship of this razor is excellent. Upon close examination, I didn't find a single scratch or blemish in the finish. Please note that although the razor itself is made in Japan, the AC adapter and the cleaning system are both made in China.<br /><br />Final thoughts: I returned this razor for a refund. Apparently, I'm just not the foil razor type. I get a faster and easier shave with a Norelco. In addition, I find the traditional Norelco razors a little easier to clean, and they cost a lot less.

  264. Ok, let's get one thing straight: this shaver is not worth an MSRP of 600 bucks. Unless it literally shaved for me - even if it shaved for me - it wouldn't be worth that kind of dough. But on Gold Box deal of the day? Well, it was still expensive. That's the only reason I took off a star; it's a relatively expensive item vs. the competition. That said, in every other aspect, I love this shaver. Pros: - A base that works!: I was hesitant to get the base, but since it was part of the gold box deal, I bit. in the past, I've used the Braun bases, which make you buy a solution that evaporates quickly. You didn't have a choice but to replace it on a regular basis. The Panasonic base has a concentrated solution that mixes with water you put into a reservoir in the base. I believe it only mixes when you set it to clean. This is obviously a big savings if you don't feel the need to use the cleaning function on a daily basis. And since this is a wet/dry shaver, you can wash it on a daily basis, and save cleanings for special occasions. It also allows you to just dry the blades and head, so it seems they anticipated this. - A close shave: Dry, it performs marginally better than my old Braun. It took some getting used to - the 5 blades make you feel like you're shaving with the side of a brick, and it feels difficult sometimes to get to the smaller parts of your face, like your upper lip. However, it is much more efficient than my old electric. Wet, however, this thing is amazing. I took it into the shower, no cream or anything, and got the closest shave I've had in years. And no burn. - Easy to clean: just pop off the screen, rinse the blades using the sonic vibrating mode, rinse the screens, pop it back on, stick it in the base to dry. You can use soap on both, or use the base cleaning. Very quick and easy. - Lock: This is handy if you pack your shaver. It locks it's ability to turn on. - Charges quick: didn't think this would be that big of a deal,but it's actually pretty handy if you travel. Cons: - Cost: Wow, this is expensive. It's expensive on sale. - Travel pouch: It is leather-like (but not really leather), so I guess one could claim it is premium in some sense, but I prefer the hard case of my previous shaver. If I'm dropping 300 bucks on a shaver, I don't want it to get inadvertently crushed in my bag. - Ergonomics: they aren't horrible, but they certainly aren't the best. It's a very head heavy shaver, so when you've rinsed it, shaking off excess water makes you feel like the head is going to come off. I have no reason to expect that it will - it is well made - but just the weight distribution gives you this sense. The floating head actually makes it difficult to shave sometimes, though there is a position lock, so if that bugs you, you can always lock it in place. - Trimmer: I guess this is partly attributed to the ergonomics, but the trimmer is underwhelming. It's slightly difficult to use, even if it cuts fine. All in all, it's a great shaver, albeit at a very high price. My gripes are a bit nit-picky; none of those are make or break problems, just annoyances. If you've got money to burn, and really need a shaver, you'd be hard pressed to find a better one.

Eighty percent is still consistent with getting 45 minutes of usage per charge. I have not tried going two weeks between charges, because I don’t want to risk having to shave with a blade. For travel, the power supply unplugs from the cleaning/drying machine and will plug into the shaver, so you could take just the shaver (it comes with a soft travel case) and the charger with you. Throw one in your suitcase and you won't have to remember to bring one with you.<br /><br />Bottom line: I look forward to shaving in the morning.<br /><br />UPDATE - JULY 2016: The cleaning station malfunctioned. Although I could clear the drain with a paper clip, it also would not run the clean cycle unless I unplugged it for a few seconds. I had an unsatisfactory customer service experience, talking to someone in the Philippines who was working from a script, and later with someone domestic. Both insisted that I had to send the entire system to them, even though the shaver works. Now, I cannot find out the status of the repair. I guess I'll wait another week and see if I receive a package from McAllen. Not a good experience for a shaver with a $600 list price. On the bright side, Amazon finally started carrying both after a long delay, although foil and cutter combined are only available through third party vendors at full retail; you're better off buying the foil and blade separately.<br /><br />Amazon's model numbers are slightly off on the model summary page, so here are the links:<br /><br />[[ASIN:B005HMOEEE Panasonic Wes9170p Replacement Inner Blade for Men's Shaver]]<br />[[ASIN:B003H9GN9S Panasonic Wes9171p Replacement Outer Foil for Men's Shaver]]<br /><br />Why am I rating this 1 star rather than the 3-4 stars of the shave versus price that would be appropriate for its overall value? Well, unfortunately, after about 10 months of use the battery will no longer hold a charge for more than a few hours. It is the weirdest battery error I've ever encountered. Most batteries will simply hold far less of a charge when they are ready for replacement; this one will hold a full charge for 60 minutes of continuous use, but if left alone overnight it will have no charge left. That's a defective design, and unlike previous Panasonic models you can't use the razorwith the cord plugged in so the razor is essentially useless if this happens.<br /><br />Despite a nominal warranty of 2 years, customer service refuses to accept this for warranty without a receipt even though this model wasn't released until late 2011. It'll be returned for warranty service eventually, but the combination of these errors means I cannot recommend this product or Panasonic customer service. Product failure like this on a exorbitantly priced flagship model is bad enough, but poor customer service means it's not something worth buying. 1 star.

Cannot rightfully compare that with the Braun since I cannot use shaving cream with it.<br /><br />Feel: I would say the Braun feels like its meant to fit in your hand better though the Panasonic is by no means bad.<br /><br />Loudness: ESLV81K is a good bit higher in pitch, which seems to just barely creep past my 2 shut doors to my sleeping girlfriend. The Braun 790cc cannot be heard with 2 doors between you and it. Its lower buzz is more enjoyable to my ears.<br /><br />Cleaning Station: The Braun's looks way better but the Panasonic's is easier to read and figure out for first timers. They both get the job done and the shavers come out as clean as when it was unboxed. Tossup here, can't decide which I prefer until I mention the cleaning solution.<br /><br />Cleaning Solution: I had to put this in a completely separate category because I don't feel the cleaning station of the Panasonic is by any means inferior to Braun's. Though the cleaning solution is just bad to me. The Braun 790cc comes out smelling lemony fresh and is so very pleasant during 90% of your shave time and the 10% of the alcohol smell while doing your upper lip isn't that bad. The Panasonic on the other hand, it smells so odd... Hard to describe better, smells soapy but not a good soapy smell. Like soap trying to cover up a mold smell. The more worn the Panasonic's cleaning cartridgeis the less obtrusive the smell is though. But 100%, Braun cleaning solution is so much better on the senses. Though I would like to repeat, they both get the shaver clean!<br /><br />Manual Clean: I know Braun gives you a brush but they shouldn't, you cannot manually clean it, don't even bother. The Panasonic's manual cleaning is easy and probably as effective as the cleaning station. Heck, I would probably recommend people get just the shaver for the Panasonic.<br /><br />Now the important stuff, the shaving experience!<br /><br />***I use Lab Series For Men Electric Shaver Solution when Dry shaving.<br /><br />Trimmer: They both stink hardcore. Choosing between a turd and a pile of poo here. If forced I would pick the Panasonic's trimmer.<br /><br />3-Day Stubble: Braun did way better than I would have thought, just some jaw hairs needed touching up. Panasonic looked just as good as 1 day stubble shaving.<br /><br />Dry Shave Experience: Both are very comfortable, feel as though I end up with more red bumps and irritation with the ESLV81K but might just be the closeness and its only around my bottom neck. Braun gives me some around my neck/jaw probably from all the skin stretching I do around that area.<br /><br />Wet Shave Experience: Only Panasonic here, have I used it with cream? Yes, I won't say much about it because I don't like using cream with shavers because I think its messy but I will say it works. I use shaving gel, a little lighter and not quite as messy. With my gel (Eshu, had to throw the brand name in there, I love their stuff), the Panasonic glides effortlessly and gets a pretty close shave. I would say it's only slightly closer than a dry shave.<br /><br />Handling: I NEED TO SAY THIS BECAUSE I WAS WORRIED A LOT BY IT! The Panasonic's 5 blade head is not as big as it looks and it fits in my 'stache area with ease. The big head doesn't off-balance the device in your hand and the maneuverability of the head is admirable. I might say it is too maneuverable and you may need to put the lock on to press down harder to get an area. The Braun feels even better though, probably because the Panasonic moves left to right as well as up and down which I feel is overkill.<br /><br />Shave Speed: Holy cow, Panasonic just destroys my facial hair. Cheeks and upper lip only need 1 pass most of the time. Neck requires an extra pass or two. Braun requires a lot more face stretching which adds up. the 790cc also needs a minimum of 3-4 strokes at one spot, the Panasonic is just way faster.<br /><br />Shave Closeness: An unholy patch of neck/jaw hair my Braun couldn't get was shaved closer by the ESLV81K but not as good as I hoped. Would have to say besides that, the difference isn't huge. Panasonic is just a little closer everywhere.<br /><br />Am I required to pick a winner? Ugh, I think I may return my ESLV81K and hope the Braun 799cc wet/dry shaver comes out this summer (had a personal response from BraunUS twitter saying it was coming out this summer)or the 790cc hits a big sale here on Amazon. I'd say the Braun wasn't worth the price but the Panasonic isn't either. Add the replacement heads of the Panasonic which, as I write this, are currently on backorder and are over $80 for the combo foil and blades! The Panasonic cleaning cartridges are cheaper in the long run but nowhere close enough to make up for the replacement heads.<br /><br />My winner comes down to the one thing I didn't want it to, price... Even if you don't mind throwing around money, the boost in shave quality with the Panasonic is so minimal that it's not worth $100 more than the Braun. Let me finish by saying, I would be keeping the Panasonic if Braun's cleaning solution didn't smell so very good.

Dear Amazon Shopper,<br /><br />There's a lot that could be said about all of the technology that goes into this razor, and a great many other reviewers have dissected every feature this gadget has to offer. I am writing this review to concisely answer the question I assume led most people to read this item's reviews: \\"Does it provide a close shave compared to other razors in its class?\\"<br /><br />Frankly, there really aren't any other razors in this class. I own a Braun Series 7 and have used a Norelco 1280X 3D on several occasions; this razor is better. The shave is smoother, it's less apt to nick you, even if you've got an irritated hair follicle or two, you can cart it into the shower with you, and the self-cleaning is thorough.<br /><br />However, you could buy both the Norelco and the Braun for the price of this razor. The question thus becomes, is the superior shave worth the stratospheric price tag? The answer depends on you. If you're willing to fork over double what the next-best electric razor costs for the closest shave an electric razor can provide, this is the razor you want. The first couple of times you use it, it will be uncomfortable and may nick you, but within a week's time your face will adjust and you'll be getting a smoother shave than you thought possible from an electronic device.<br /><br />Otherwise, the Braun is a fine alternative for a dry shave at half the price.<br /><br />Bottom Line: The best electric shave money can buy at twice the price of the nearest competitor.
